Jamison Brereton

65 (777)
Soma Pavama╠Дna
Bhrgu V ╠е ─Бruс╣Зi or Jamadagni Bh─Бrgava
30 verses: g─Бyatr─л, arranged in trcas ╠е
Even in this maс╣Зс╕Нala devoted to тАЬself-purifyingтАЭ Soma, the constant repetition of that epithet and its associated verbal forms (тАЬpurify yourself,тАЭ etc.) in this hymn is remarkable. In particular, the idiom тАЬby purifying yourself bring here …тАЭ (much more economically expressed in Sanskrit by ─Б╠Б pavasva) is insistent, along with other demands that Soma bring or convey goods here. Intermingled are verses treating the familiar details of soma preparation. All in all, the hymn seems flat, uninspired, and repetitive.
The tr╠еca consisting of verses 22тАУ24 breaks the monotony to some degree, with the first two verses listing various places where the soma may be pressed (the meaning of some of these words is disputed and their translation provisional), and only the third returning to the dominant theme of the hymn. The final tr╠еca (vss. 28тАУ30) brings the hymn to a close with a flurry of repetitions of the preverb ─Б╠Б тАЬhere, hither,тАЭ in a list of items we wish to bring to hand as a result of the soma offering.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On the qualities of this hymn as a whole, see published introduction.

61-67 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

On the place of these long hymns in the structure of the maс╣Зс╕Нala, see published introduction. to IX.61. All of these hymns consist of collections of tс╣Ыcas of varying degrees of cohesion. In fact, it is surprising how few tс╣Ыcas display a real attempt at thematic or lexical unity, and what they do show is often simply the byproduct of the fact that both the lexicon and thematic preoccupations of Maс╣Зс╕Нala IX are comparatively limited and so similar words and themes are not unlikely to show up in adjacent verses. This lack of unity contrasts, I think (this is my unsystematic and anecdotal impression) with collections of tс╣Ыcas in other maс╣Зс╕Нalas, notably VIII.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe kindred fingers diligently operating, eager to squeeze you forth, send out the invigorating the lord (of all), the mighty Indu.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The rosy (fingers) impel the sun; the kindred sisters impel their lord; those seeking the great impel the great drop.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The identification of Soma with the Sun, noted passim above in the last two hymns, here begins the hymn.

The tr. тАЬrosy (fingers)тАЭ is of course an unauthorized allusion to HomerтАЩs тАЬrosyfingered dawnтАЭ - though it is more legitimate than it might first appear. The word tr. тАШrosyтАЩ, ├║sri-, is ultimately derived from the тАШdawnтАЩ word; cf. the related usr├б-, usr├нya-, both of which are color terms representing the light of dawn (тАШruddyтАЩ) generally applied to bovines.

The next p─Бda, with its fem. subj. sv├бs─Бro j─Бm├бyaс╕е тАЬkindred sistersтАЭ is a standard way of referring to the fingers of the priests that prepare the soma (cf., e.g., IX.89.4). Thus the first two p─Бdas superimpose two images: the ruddy Dawn(s) impelling the sun, the fingers impelling the soma - allowing each to participate in the imagery of the other. Because of the erotic relationship sometimes depicted between Dawn and the Sun, it would be better to tr.

p├бtim in b as тАЬtheir husbandтАЭ (with Geldner, Renou), not тАШlordтАЩ as in the published translation - making one more link between the imagery of p─Бdas a and b.

Note that Geldner nodded (slightly) in tr. mah─Б╠Бn ├нndum as тАЬden grossen Indra,тАЭ enabled by the constant association between those two words in IX.

01-03 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

No particular signs of unity. Vss. 2 and 3 have forms of the pres. part.

p├бvam─Бna- and 3 also the impv. ─Б╠БтАж pavasva, but esp. in this hymn, the appearance of these forms is hardly noteworthy. Vss. 2 and 3 also have dev├йbhyaс╕е in their b p─Бdas, but in different cases.

Griffith

THE, glittering maids send Sura forth, the glorious sisters, close-allied,
Send Indu forth, their mighty Lord.

Geldner

Die morgendlichen treiben die Sonne zur Eile, die versippten Schwestern den Gatten, den gro├Яen Indra, sich geehrt f├╝hlend.

Grassmann

Die Sonne senden morgenhell, den Gatten die verschwisterten, Den grossen Indu grossgesinnt.

O self-purifying one, with light after light, as god from among the gods, enter all good things.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPour, purified (Soma), a well-praised shower for the worship of the gods; (pour) a continual shower for our food.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

O self-purifying one, by purifying yourself bring here good praise, rain, and friendship from the gods,
continuously for refreshment.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Both Geldner and Renou take dev├йbhyaс╕е as dat. with d├║vaс╕е: тАЬEifer f├╝r die G├╢tter,тАЭ тАЬlтАЩhommage aux dieux,тАЭ whereas in the published translation I take it as an abl., тАЬfriendship from the gods.тАЭ The issue is the multivalence of d├║vas- and its derivatives; in the meaning тАШfriendshipтАЩ it generally refers to the mutually agreeable relationship between men and gods.

In this context it seemed to me odd to order Soma to тАЬbring [us] through purificationтАЭ friendship for the gods, hence my ablatival interpr. However, a more detailed examination of the usage of d├║vas- and the denom. duvasy├б- shows that the offering / seeking of d├║vasgenerally goes from men to gods (or Agni, as the god closest to men, to gods). E.g., dev├йс╣гu kс╣Ыс╣Зuto d├║vaс╕е тАЬThe two [= married couple] do friendly service to the godsтАЭ; III.3.1 agn├нr h├н dev─Б╠Бm╠Рamс╣Ы╠Бto duvasyati тАЬFor Agni the immortal does friendly service to / befriends the gods.тАЭ I therefore would emend the tr. to datival тАЬbring тАж friendship for the gods.тАЭ Like the parallel obj. suс╣гс╣нut├нm тАШgood praiseтАЩ, d├║vas- is then something that we mortals offer to the gods, but, though it originates from us, it is Soma who stimulates our production of these offerings, hence ─Б╠БтАж pavasva тАЬbring by purifying yourself.тАЭ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWell-armed (Soma) who does exhilarate (the gods) pour forth for us male offspring; come, Indu, favourably to our sacrifice.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Well-armed: or, having fine sacrificial implements, such as sphya, kap─Бla

By purifying yourself bring here an abundance of heroes, you yourself becoming exhilarated, o you of good weapons.
Come just here, o drop. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

The vs. contains an address (in pl.) to priest-singers to sing (g─Бyata), with comparison to a previous singer Vya┼Ыva (vya┼Ыvav├бt тАШlike Vya┼ЫvaтАЩ) who did the same. Why Vya┼Ыva appears here is something of a mystery. Aside from a bare mention in an A┼Ыvin list hymn (I.112.15), Vya┼Ыva is found only in VIII, where he is identified as a с╣Ыс╣гi (VIII.9.10, 23.10) and his descendants receive the dakс╣гiс╣З─Б at the end of the sacrifice (VIII.24.28-29).

The adv. vya┼Ыvav├бt тАШlike Vya┼ЫvaтАЩ is found 3x in that little group of hymns in VIII (23-26), attributed in the Anukramaс╣З─л to one of his descendents, Vi┼Ыvamanas Vaiya┼Ыva. I donтАЩt know why he should surface once in IX; our hymn is not attributed to him or any of his obvious relatives (rather to Bhс╣Ыgu V─Бruс╣Зi or Jamadagni Bh─Бrgava), and there is nothing particularly somic about his appearances in VIII - though his descendents may once be called som├нn- тАШhaving or providing somaтАЭ (VIII.24.29; see comm. ad loc.). He is more closely associated with the A┼Ыvins (I.112.15 just mentioned; VIII.9.10, 26.9 [both A┼Ыvin hymns]).

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(That Soma) whose juice they squeeze out with the stones, foe-repelling, honey-dropping, green-tinted, for Indra to drink.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Him whose tawny hue, dripping with honey, they impel (like) a fallow bay with the stones,
the drop for Indra to drink,

Jamison Brereton Notes

The construction of the first hemistich is somewhat tricky. The rel. y├бsya must refer to soma, with the rel. cl. hanging off vs. 7. In p─Бda a the y├бsya qualifies v├бrс╣Зam тАШcolorтАЩ, which serves as obj. of hinv├бnti in b. тАЬThey impel his colorтАЭ is a slightly odd locution, and it becomes odder in b, with the acc. h├бrim. The stem h├бri- is a color term and could qualify v├бrс╣Зa- (тАЬtawny colorтАЭ), but it also is regularly applied directly to soma (e.g., in vss. 12 and 25 of this hymn) and also identifies IndraтАЩs horse(s). Geldner (n. 8b) cleverly suggests that h├бri- is to be read twice, with the second reading an unmarked simile referring to a horse of the appropriate color. This provides a more appropriate obj. for hinv├бnti (тАЬthey impel (like) a fallow bay (horse)тАЭ), while connecting the putative horse with the тАЬtawny colorтАЭ (v├бrс╣Зam тАж h├бrim) that is the 1st obj. of the verb.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬFlow in a stream, you who are the showerer (of benefits); and (be) exhilarating to the lord of the Maruts granting us all (wealth) by your power.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

As bull purify yourself in a stream, and as exhilarating drink for the one accompanied by the Maruts [=Indra],
making all things your own by your strength.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The function of the ca in b is unclear. Klein (DGRV I.256-57) discusses three possible explanations - GeldnerтАЩs, RenouтАЩs, and one of his own - of which he prefers RenouтАЩs: that mar├║tvate ca conceals an ellipsis тАЬ(for the Maruts) and (for Indra) accompanied by the Maruts,тАЭ which seems by far the least likely and the most cumbersome. Among other things, the Maruts barely figure in IX (though cf. vs. 20 below), and I also know of no passages containing mar├║tvant- that also contain a free form of mar├║t-. My solution is admittedly makeshift but simpler, that cs conjoins the disharmonious dh─Б╠Бray─Б тАЬin a streamтАЭ and mar├║tvate тАж matsar├бс╕е тАЬexhilarating drink for Indra.тАЭ This is closest to GeldnerтАЩs, criticized by Klein as assuming тАЬa harsh conjunction in p─Бdas a and b.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The king is sped by (words of) wisdom, purifying himself in ManuтАЩs presence,
to drive through the midspace.

Jamison Brereton Notes

─лyate is assigned to тИЪy─Б/─л тАШimplore, beseechтАЩ by numerous scholars, incl. Grassmann, Lubotsky, and L├╝ders (214-15: тАЬDer K├╢nig wird mit Liedern gebetenтАЭ), though Geldner, Renou and the published translation

take it to тИЪy─Б/─л тАШspeedтАЩ (so also S─Бyaс╣Зa., who glosses gacchati). In favor of the latter, Renou declares that ─лyate is always тАЬil sтАЩavanceтАЭ in IX. I would also point out 1) the king is definitely traveling in p─Бda c (y─Б╠Бtave, to the same root) and 2) the тАШis spedтАЩ interpr. is supported by a passage like IX.26.3 t├бс╣Г vedh─Б╠Бm medh├бy─Б╠Бhyan тАЬThey impelled the ritual adept with their wisdomтАЭ also containing an instr. of medh─Б╠Б- with a clear indication of movement (ahyan). Kulikov (495-96) discusses both root possibilities without seeming to decide, though the fact that he lists it with 2 y─Б (─л) тАШimplore, requestтАЩ probably indicates his choice.

┼Ыatagv├нnam g├бv─Бm p├│с╣гam, lit. тАЬthriving of cattle that possesses hundredfold cattleтАЭ (vel sim.), redundantly codes the cattle twice (-gv├нnam g├бv─Бm).

English translation:

тАЬ(Be) expressed for the banquet of the gods;bestow on us, Soma, strength, speed and a form for brilliance.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Bring to us here, o Soma, strength and speed, as if in physical form, for luster,
when you have been pressed to seek the gods.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The s-stem neut. j├║vas- is a hapax, contrasting with the more conventionally formed and somewhat better attested j├бvas-. The zero-gr. root syllable is of course anomalous (see AiG II.2.232, without explanation), though see nearby d├║vaс╕е (vs. 3b), whatever its source. It may owe its form (or have been encouraged in maintaining its form) by the properly formed homonymous root noun pl. (vayo-)j├║vaс╕е (to -j┼л╠Б-) in the same metrical position in 26a below, as well as the aforementioned d├║vaс╕е also in the same position in 3b (cf. also ─Бbh├║vaс╕е 27a, mayobh├║vam 28a). A somewhat similar explan. is given by Renou Given the contextual triggers in this passage, it is probably wise not to invest too much in a deep diachronic account of the anomalous root syllable.

The simile in b, r┼лp├бс╣Г n├б (or r┼лp├бс╣Г n├б v├бrcase), is difficult to interpr. Geldner simply renders it literally тАЬwie Sch├╢nheit unserem Aussehen,тАЭ but it is unclear to me what the basis of comparison is. RenouтАЩs rendering goes to the opposite extreme, with a flurry of parentheses: тАЬcomme (on ajoute) la forme-concr├иte pour (donner) l’├йclat (├а une id├йe).тАЭ My own interpr.

arises from the parallelism between vss. 17 and 18. In the former we ask Soma to bring material goods, esp. livestock. Here in p─Бda a we request abstract qualities, тАЬstrength and speed,тАЭ and I suggest that r┼лp├бс╣Г n├б тАЬas if (in) physical formтАЭ is assimiliating them to the material goods of the previous vs. RenouтАЩs alt. interpr., given at the end of his n., тАЬapporte-nous force et vitesse, tel un objet-concret,тАЭ is similar and preferable to his more elaborate first interpr.

Like beauty for a brilliant show.

The soma juices that have been pressed in the distance, those nearby, or those yonder in a reed-filled (lake),

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first two p─Бdas contain antonymic locations.

The location in c is taken by Geldner/Renou as a place name, тАЬin ┼Ъaryaс╣З─Бvat,тАЭ but a place descriptor seems preferable, given the other locative expressions in these vss. On the word see comm. ad VIII.6.39 and Thieme, Unters. p. 40 n. 2.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, this tс╣Ыca is thematically unified by a listing of the many place in which soma can be pressed in 22-23; all these clauses share a single verb sunvir├й in 22b. The two vss. are followed by a summary vs. (24) expressing the hope that all these diverse soma types will bring good things to us. The tс╣Ыca also shows signs of formal cohesion that are rare in these G─Бyatr─л assemblages: vss. 22-23 consist of six p─Бda-length rel. cl., all introduced by y├й, with disjunctive v─Б found in both c p─Бdas, while 24 begins with the resumptive and summarizing correlative t├й.

тАЬOr among the с╣Ъjikas, or the Kс╣Ыtvas, or in the neighbourhood of the rivers Sarasvat─л, or in the five castes.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Jamison Brereton

Those (pressed) in foamy (places) among performers (of rituals), those in the middle of dwelling places,
or those among the five peoples,

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner and Renou (see also Mayr. PN s.vv.) take ─Бrj─лk├йс╣гu and kс╣Ы╠Бtvasu as referring to peoples. On ─Бrj─лk├б- see comm. ad VIII.7.29 and Thieme, Unters. p. 40 n. 2. As for kс╣Ы╠Бtvan-, since in its other two occurrences in the RV (VIII.24.25, X.144.3) it is adjectival, in the meaning тАШactive, enterprisingтАЩ, I see no reason why it should be a proper noun only here. I was tempted to tr. it тАЬritually active,тАЭ but this came uncomfortably close to тАЬsexually active.тАЭ As for pasty─Б╠А- as тАШdwelling placeтАЩ, rather than тАШriverтАЩ (Geldner, Renou, etc.), see comm. ad I.40.7 and IX.97.18.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, this tс╣Ыca is thematically unified by a listing of the many place in which soma can be pressed in 22-23; all these clauses share a single verb sunvir├й in 22b. The two vss. are followed by a summary vs. (24) expressing the hope that all these diverse soma types will bring good things to us. The tс╣Ыca also shows signs of formal cohesion that are rare in these G─Бyatr─л assemblages: vss. 22-23 consist of six p─Бda-length rel. cl., all introduced by y├й, with disjunctive v─Б found in both c p─Бdas, while 24 begins with the resumptive and summarizing correlative t├й.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, this tс╣Ыca is thematically unified by a listing of the many place in which soma can be pressed in 22-23; all these clauses share a single verb sunvir├й in 22b. The two vss. are followed by a summary vs. (24) expressing the hope that all these diverse soma types will bring good things to us. The tс╣Ыca also shows signs of formal cohesion that are rare in these G─Бyatr─л assemblages: vss. 22-23 consist of six p─Бda-length rel. cl., all introduced by y├й, with disjunctive v─Б found in both c p─Бdas, while 24 begins with the resumptive and summarizing correlative t├й.

English translation:

тАЬThe delightful green-tinted Soma, praised by Jamadagni, urged on the cow-hide flows (to the vessels).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

He purifies himself, the delightful tawny one, while being hymned by Jamadagni
and being impelled onto the hide of the cow.

Jamison Brereton Notes

haryat├│ h├бriс╕е тАЬdelightful tawny oneтАЭ is a word play, with two semantically different stems. This same word play is the focus of a whole hymn, III.44, and obviously was a staple of RVic phraseology.

English translation:

тАЬThe bright Soma-juices, the dispensers of food, being mixed with the curds and milk, are cleansed in the waters like horses urged (by the charioteers).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The dispensers of food: Soma grants all the boons in the hope of which the worshipper offers the Soma to the gods

Jamison Brereton

Forth (go) the clear (soma juices), speeding with vigor, being impelled like teams.
Being brought to readiness, they are groomed in the waters.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On the relationship of vayoj├║vaс╕е in p─Бda a and s├бho j├║vaс╕е in 18a, see comm. ad 18 above. Scarlatta (174) hesitates between act. and pass. meaning for this hapax rt. noun cmpd vayo-j┼л╠Б-: тАЬdie Lebenskraft f├╢rdendenтАЭ / тАЬvon Kraft beschleunigten.тАЭ In the published translation I opt for an intrans. + instr. value: тАЬspeeding with vigor,тАЭ though I now think passive тАЬsped by vigorтАЭ would be even better, on the basis of the clear pass. forms in context (hinv─Бn─Б╠Бsaс╕е тАж ┼Ыr─лс╣З─Бn─Б╠Бс╕е тАж mс╣Ы├▒jata) as well as a passage in the immediately preceding hymn, IX.64.16 pr├б hinv─Бn─Б╠Бsaс╕е … dhiy─Б╠Бj┼лt─Б╠Бс╕е тАЬBeing impelled forth тАж sped by insightful thoughts,тАЭ with the passive ppl. j┼лt├б-.
